<p>The <b>Christian Democratic Union of Germany</b> (<a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">German</a>: <span lang="de"><i>Christlich Demokratische Union Deutschlands</i></span>, <b>CDU</b>; <small>German pronunciation:</small> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_German" title="Help:IPA for German">[ˈkʁɪstlɪç ˌdemoˈkʁaːtɪʃə uˈni̯oːn ˈdɔʏtʃlants]</a></span>) is a <a href="/wiki/Christian_democracy" title="Christian democracy">Christian democratic</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nordsieck_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-Nordsieck-7">[7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Banchoff_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-Banchoff-8">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AnttiroikoM.C3.A4lki.C3.A42007_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-AnttiroikoM.C3.A4lki.C3.A42007-9">[9]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Liberal_conservatism" title="Liberal conservatism">liberal-conservative</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nordsieck_7-1"><a href="#cite_note-Nordsieck-7">[7]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/List_of_political_parties_in_Germany" title="List of political parties in Germany">political party</a> in <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a>. It is the major <a href="/wiki/Big_tent" title="Big tent">catch-all party</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Centre-right_politics" title="Centre-right politics">centre-right</a> in German politics.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-KesselmanKrieger2008_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-KesselmanKrieger2008-10">[10]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wiliarty2010_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-Wiliarty2010-11">[11]</a></sup> The CDU forms the <a href="/wiki/CDU/CSU" title="CDU/CSU">CDU/CSU</a> grouping, also known as the Union, in the <a href="/wiki/Bundestag" title="Bundestag">Bundestag</a> with its Bavarian counterpart the <a href="/wiki/Christian_Social_Union_in_Bavaria" title="Christian Social Union in Bavaria">Christian Social Union in Bavaria</a> (CSU).</p>
<p>The leader of the CDU, <a href="/wiki/Angela_Merkel" title="Angela Merkel">Angela Merkel</a>, is the current <a href="/wiki/Chancellor_of_Germany" title="Chancellor of Germany">Chancellor of Germany</a>. The CDU is a member of the <a href="/wiki/Centrist_Democrat_International" title="Centrist Democrat International">Centrist Democrat International</a>, <a href="/wiki/International_Democrat_Union" title="International Democrat Union">International Democrat Union</a> and <a href="/wiki/European_People%27s_Party" title="European People's Party">European People's Party</a> (EPP).</p>
<p></p>

</div>
<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Christian_Democratic_Union_of_Germany&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Immediately following the collapse of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nazi" title="Nazi">Nazi</a> <a href="/wiki/Dictatorship" title="Dictatorship">dictatorship</a> at the end of <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, the need for a new political order in <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a> was paramount. Simultaneous yet unrelated meetings began occurring throughout Germany, each with the intention of planning a "Christian-democratic party". The "Christlich-Demokratische Union" was established in <a href="/wiki/Berlin" title="Berlin">Berlin</a> on 26 June 1945, and in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rheinland" title="Rheinland">Rheinland</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Westfalen" title="Westfalen">Westfalen</a> in September of the same year.</p>
<p>The founding members of the CDU consisted primarily of former members of the <a href="/wiki/Centre_Party_(Germany)" title="Centre Party (Germany)">Centre Party</a>, <a href="/wiki/German_Democratic_Party" title="German Democratic Party">German Democratic Party</a>, <a href="/wiki/German_National_People%27s_Party" title="German National People's Party">German National People's Party</a>, and <a href="/wiki/German_People%27s_Party" title="German People's Party">German People's Party</a>. Many of these individuals, including CDU-Berlin founder <a href="/wiki/Andreas_Hermes" title="Andreas Hermes">Andreas Hermes</a> and future chancellor of Germany <a href="/wiki/Konrad_Adenauer" title="Konrad Adenauer">Konrad Adenauer</a>, were imprisoned for the involvement in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/German_Resistance" title="German Resistance">German Resistance</a> during the Nazi dictatorship. In the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a> years, after World War II up to the <a href="/wiki/Vergangenheitsbew%C3%A4ltigung#After_denazification" title="Vergangenheitsbewältigung">1960s</a>, the CDU also attracted conservative, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anti-Communist" title="Anti-Communist">anti-Communist</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Former_Nazis" title="Former Nazis">former Nazis</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nazi_collaborators" title="Nazi collaborators">Nazi collaborators</a> into its higher ranks (like <a href="/wiki/Hans_Globke" title="Hans Globke">Hans Globke</a> and <a href="/wiki/Theodor_Oberl%C3%A4nder" title="Theodor Oberländer">Theodor Oberländer</a>). A prominent anti-Nazi member was theologian <a href="/wiki/Eugen_Gerstenmaier" title="Eugen Gerstenmaier">Eugen Gerstenmaier</a> who became Acting Chairman of the Foreign Board (1949-1969).</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:CDU_Wahlkampfplakat_-_kaspl019.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2939" data-file-width="2056" height="314" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/CDU_Wahlkampfplakat_-_kaspl019.JPG/220px-CDU_Wahlkampfplakat_-_kaspl019.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/CDU_Wahlkampfplakat_-_kaspl019.JPG/330px-CDU_Wahlkampfplakat_-_kaspl019.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/CDU_Wahlkampfplakat_-_kaspl019.JPG/440px-CDU_Wahlkampfplakat_-_kaspl019.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:CDU_Wahlkampfplakat_-_kaspl019.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The election poster of 1957: "No experiments", featuring then Chancellor <a href="/wiki/Konrad_Adenauer" title="Konrad Adenauer">Konrad Adenauer</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>One of the lessons learned from the failure of the <a href="/wiki/Weimar_Republic" title="Weimar Republic">Weimar Republic</a> was that disunity among the democratic parties ultimately allowed for the rise of the <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Party" title="Nazi Party">Nazi Party</a>. It was therefore crucial to create a unified party of Christian Democrats – a Christian Democratic "Union". The result of these meetings was the establishment of an inter-confessional (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Catholic" title="Catholic">Catholic</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Protestant" title="Protestant">Protestant</a> alike) party influenced heavily by the political tradition of <a href="/wiki/Liberal_conservatism" title="Liberal conservatism">liberal conservatism</a>. The CDU experienced considerable success gaining support from the time of its creation in Berlin on 26 June 1945 until its first <a href="/wiki/Political_convention" title="Political convention">convention</a> on 21 October 1950, at which Chancellor Adenauer was named the first <a href="/wiki/Chairman" title="Chairman">Chairman</a> of the party.</p>
<p>In the beginning, it was not clear which party would be favored by the victors of the Second World War, but by the end of the 1940s, the governments of the United States and of Britain began to lean toward the CDU and away from the <a href="/wiki/Social_Democratic_Party_of_Germany" title="Social Democratic Party of Germany">Social Democratic Party of Germany</a> (SPD). The latter was more nationalist and sought German reunification, even at the expense of concessions to the Soviet Union, depicting Adenauer as an instrument of both the Americans and the Vatican. The Western powers appreciated the CDU's moderation, its economic flexibility and its value as an oppositional force to the Communists, which appealed to European voters at the time. Also, Adenauer was trusted by the British.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gottfried_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-gottfried-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<p>The party was split over issues of rearmament within the Western alliance and German unification as a neutral state. Adenauer staunchly defended his pro-Western position and outmanoeuvred some of his opponents. He also refused to consider the SPD as a party of the coalition until he felt sure that they shared his anti-Communist position. The principled rejection of a reunification that would alienate Germany from the Western alliance made it harder to attract Protestant voters to the party, as most refugees from the former German territories east of the Oder were of that faith, as were the majority of the inhabitants of East Germany.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gottfried_12-1"><a href="#cite_note-gottfried-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<p>The CDU was the dominant party for the first two decades following the establishment of <a href="/wiki/West_Germany" title="West Germany">West Germany</a> in 1949. Konrad Adenauer remained the party’s leader until 1963, at which point the former minister of economics <a href="/wiki/Ludwig_Erhard" title="Ludwig Erhard">Ludwig Erhard</a> replaced him.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> As the <a href="/wiki/Free_Democratic_Party_(Germany)" title="Free Democratic Party (Germany)">Free Democratic Party</a> (FDP) withdrew from the governing coalition in 1966 due to disagreements over fiscal and economic policy, Erhard was forced to resign. Consequently, a <a href="/wiki/Grand_coalition" title="Grand coalition">grand coalition</a> with the SPD took over government under CDU Chancellor <a href="/wiki/Kurt_Georg_Kiesinger" title="Kurt Georg Kiesinger">Kurt Georg Kiesinger</a>.</p>
<p>The SPD quickly gained popularity and succeeded in forming a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Social-liberal_coalition" title="Social-liberal coalition">social-liberal coalition</a> with the FDP following the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/German_federal_election,_1969" title="German federal election, 1969">1969 federal election</a>, forcing the CDU out of power for the first time in their history. The CDU continued its role as <a href="/wiki/Opposition_(politics)" title="Opposition (politics)">opposition</a> until 1982, when the FDP’s withdrawal from the coalition with the SPD allowed the CDU to regain power.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Kohl_era">Kohl era</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Christian_Democratic_Union_of_Germany&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Kohl era">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>CDU Chairman <a href="/wiki/Helmut_Kohl" title="Helmut Kohl">Helmut Kohl</a> became the new Chancellor of West Germany and his CDU-FDP coalition was confirmed in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/German_federal_election,_1983" title="German federal election, 1983">1983 federal election</a>. Public support for the coalition's work in the process of <a href="/wiki/German_reunification" title="German reunification">German reunification</a> was reiterated in the <a href="/wiki/German_federal_election,_1990" title="German federal election, 1990">1990 federal election</a>, in which the CDU-FDP governing coalition experienced a clear victory.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-1990-0518-028,_Staatsvertrag_BRD-DDR,_Helmut_Kohl,_Lothar_de_Maizi%C3%A8re.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="528" data-file-width="800" height="145" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-1990-0518-028%2C_Staatsvertrag_BRD-DDR%2C_Helmut_Kohl%2C_Lothar_de_Maizi%C3%A8re.jpg/220px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-1990-0518-028%2C_Staatsvertrag_BRD-DDR%2C_Helmut_Kohl%2C_Lothar_de_Maizi%C3%A8re.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-1990-0518-028%2C_Staatsvertrag_BRD-DDR%2C_Helmut_Kohl%2C_Lothar_de_Maizi%C3%A8re.jpg/330px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-1990-0518-028%2C_Staatsvertrag_BRD-DDR%2C_Helmut_Kohl%2C_Lothar_de_Maizi%C3%A8re.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-1990-0518-028%2C_Staatsvertrag_BRD-DDR%2C_Helmut_Kohl%2C_Lothar_de_Maizi%C3%A8re.jpg/440px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-1990-0518-028%2C_Staatsvertrag_BRD-DDR%2C_Helmut_Kohl%2C_Lothar_de_Maizi%C3%A8re.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-1990-0518-028,_Staatsvertrag_BRD-DDR,_Helmut_Kohl,_Lothar_de_Maizi%C3%A8re.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
East German CDU leader <a href="/wiki/Lothar_de_Maizi%C3%A8re" title="Lothar de Maizière">Lothar de Maizière</a> (left) with West German CDU leader Helmut Kohl, September 1990</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>After the <a href="/wiki/Die_Wende" title="Die Wende">collapse</a> of the <a href="/wiki/East_Germany" title="East Germany">East German</a> government in 1989, Kohl – supported by the governments of the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>, and (<a href="/wiki/German_reunification#Britain_and_France" title="German reunification">reluctantly</a>) by those of <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a> and the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a> – called for <a href="/wiki/German_reunification" title="German reunification">German reunification</a>. On 3 October 1990, the German Democratic Republic (GDR) was abolished and its territory annexed by West Germany. The <a href="/wiki/Christian_Democratic_Union_(East_Germany)" title="Christian Democratic Union (East Germany)">East German CDU</a> merged with its West German counterpart, and elections were held for the reunified country. Although Kohl was re-elected, the party began losing much of its popularity because of an economic recession in the former GDR and increased taxes in the west. The CDU was, however, able to win the <a href="/wiki/German_federal_election,_1994" title="German federal election, 1994">1994 federal election</a> by a narrow margin due to an economic recovery.</p>
<p>Helmut Kohl served as chairman until the party's electoral defeat in 1998, when he was succeeded by <a href="/wiki/Wolfgang_Sch%C3%A4uble" title="Wolfgang Schäuble">Wolfgang Schäuble</a>; Schäuble resigned in early 2000 as a result of a party <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1999_CDU_contributions_scandal" title="1999 CDU contributions scandal">financing scandal</a> and was replaced by <a href="/wiki/Angela_Merkel" title="Angela Merkel">Angela Merkel</a>, who remains the leader of the CDU to this day. In the <a href="/wiki/German_federal_election,_1998" title="German federal election, 1998">1998 federal election</a>, the CDU polled 28.4% and the CSU 6.7% of the national vote, which was the lowest result for CDU/CSU since 1949. Thus, a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Red-green_alliance" title="Red-green alliance">Red-Green coalition</a> under the leadership of Gerhard Schröder took power until 2005. In 2002, the CDU and CSU polled slightly higher – 29.5% and 9.0%, respectively – but still lacked the majority needed for a CDU-FDP coalition government.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Merkel_Era">Merkel Era</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Christian_Democratic_Union_of_Germany&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Merkel Era">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Angela_Merkel_CDU_Parteitag_2014_by_Olaf_Kosinsky-25.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2132" data-file-width="2619" height="179" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Angela_Merkel_CDU_Parteitag_2014_by_Olaf_Kosinsky-25.jpg/220px-Angela_Merkel_CDU_Parteitag_2014_by_Olaf_Kosinsky-25.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Angela_Merkel_CDU_Parteitag_2014_by_Olaf_Kosinsky-25.jpg/330px-Angela_Merkel_CDU_Parteitag_2014_by_Olaf_Kosinsky-25.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Angela_Merkel_CDU_Parteitag_2014_by_Olaf_Kosinsky-25.jpg/440px-Angela_Merkel_CDU_Parteitag_2014_by_Olaf_Kosinsky-25.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Angela_Merkel_CDU_Parteitag_2014_by_Olaf_Kosinsky-25.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Angela Merkel</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 2005 early elections were called after the CDU dealt the governing SPD a major blow, winning more than ten state elections, most of which were <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_landslide_victories" title="List of landslide victories">landslide victories</a>. The resulting <a href="/wiki/Grand_coalition" title="Grand coalition">grand coalition</a> between the CDU/CSU and the SPD faced a serious challenge stemming from both parties' demand for the chancellorship. After three weeks of negotiations, however, the two parties reached a deal whereby CDU received the chancellorship while the SPD retained 8 of the 16 seats in the cabinet and a majority of the most prestigious cabinet posts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> The coalition deal was approved by both parties at party conferences on November 14.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> Merkel was confirmed as the first female Chancellor of Germany by the majority of delegates (397 to 217) in the newly assembled Bundestag on 22 November.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup></p>
<p>Although the CDU/CSU lost support in the <a href="/wiki/German_federal_election,_2009" title="German federal election, 2009">2009 federal elections</a>, the FDP experienced the best election cycle in their history, thereby enabling a CDU/CSU-FDP coalition. This marked the first change of coalition partner by a Chancellor in German history.</p>
<p>The loss of anti-Communism as a political theme, secularization, and the <a href="/wiki/Culture_war" title="Culture war">cultural revolutions</a> occurring since the 1960s have challenged the viability of the CDU. In her 2005 campaign, Angela Merkel was unwilling to express explicitly Christian views, while maintaining that her party had never lost its "concept of values". Merkel and Bundestag President <a href="/wiki/Norbert_Lammert" title="Norbert Lammert">Norbert Lammert</a> have been keen to clarify that CDU references to the "dominant culture" imply "tolerance and living together".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gottfried_12-2"><a href="#cite_note-gottfried-12">[12]</a></sup> According to party analyst <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Stephan_Eisel&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Stephan Eisel (page does not exist)">Stephan Eisel</a> however, her avoiding the values-issue may have had the opposite effect as she failed to mobilize the party's core constituency.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:CDU_Bundesgeschaeftsstelle_Berlin.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="734" height="180" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/CDU_Bundesgeschaeftsstelle_Berlin.jpg/220px-CDU_Bundesgeschaeftsstelle_Berlin.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/CDU_Bundesgeschaeftsstelle_Berlin.jpg/330px-CDU_Bundesgeschaeftsstelle_Berlin.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/CDU_Bundesgeschaeftsstelle_Berlin.jpg/440px-CDU_Bundesgeschaeftsstelle_Berlin.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:CDU_Bundesgeschaeftsstelle_Berlin.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Konrad-Adenauer-Haus, headquarters of the CDU, in <a href="/wiki/Berlin" title="Berlin">Berlin</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>While Adenauer and Erhard co-operated with non-Nazi parties to their right, later the CDU has worked to marginalize its right-wing opposition.</p>

<ul>

<li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Christian_democracy_sidebar&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li>

<p>The CDU applying the principles of <a href="/wiki/Christian_democracy" title="Christian democracy">Christian democracy</a> and emphasising the "Christian understanding of humans and their responsibility toward God." CDU membership consists however of people adhering to a variety of religions as well as non-religious individuals. The CDU's policies derive from <a href="/wiki/Political_Catholicism" title="Political Catholicism">political Catholicism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Catholic_social_teaching" title="Catholic social teaching">Catholic social teaching</a> and political <a href="/wiki/Protestantism" title="Protestantism">Protestantism</a>, as well as <a href="/wiki/Fiscal_conservatism" title="Fiscal conservatism">fiscal conservatism</a> and <a href="/wiki/National_conservatism" title="National conservatism">national conservatism</a>. The CDU was the first proponent of the <a href="/wiki/Social_market_economy" title="Social market economy">social market economy</a><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>, although the party has adopted more <a href="/wiki/Economic_liberalism" title="Economic liberalism">liberal economic</a> policies since <a href="/wiki/Helmut_Kohl" title="Helmut Kohl">Helmut Kohl</a>'s term in office as the Chancellor of Germany (1982–1998).</p>
<p>As a <a href="/wiki/Conservatism" title="Conservatism">conservative</a> party, the CDU supports stronger punishments of crimes and supports involvement on the part of the <a href="/wiki/Bundeswehr" title="Bundeswehr">Bundeswehr</a> in cases of domestic <a href="/wiki/Counter-terrorism" title="Counter-terrorism">anti-terrorism</a> offensives. In terms of immigrants, the CDU supports initiatives to integrate immigrants through language courses, and aims to further control immigration. <a href="/wiki/Multiple_citizenship" title="Multiple citizenship">Dual citizenship</a> should only be allowed in exceptional cases. The CDU emphasises curtailing <a href="/wiki/Red_tape" title="Red tape">red tape</a> and the preservation of cultural traditions.</p>
<p>In terms of foreign policy, the CDU commits itself to <a href="/wiki/European_integration" title="European integration">European integration</a> and a strong relation with the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>. In the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>, the party opposes the entry of <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a> into the EU, preferring instead a privileged partnership with <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a>. In addition to citing various human rights violations, the CDU also believes that Turkey's unwillingness to recognise <a href="/wiki/Cyprus" title="Cyprus">Cyprus</a> as an independent, sovereign state contradicts the EU policy that its members must recognise the existence of one another.</p>
<p>Opponents of the CDU are the <a href="/wiki/Social_Democratic_Party_of_Germany" title="Social Democratic Party of Germany">Social Democratic Party of Germany</a> (SPD), <a href="/wiki/The_Left_(Germany)" title="The Left (Germany)">The Left</a> party and <a href="/wiki/Alliance_%2790/The_Greens" title="Alliance '90/The Greens">Alliance '90/The Greens</a>. The CDU has however governed in three federal-level and numerous state-level <a href="/wiki/Grand_coalition_(Germany)" title="Grand coalition (Germany)">Grand Coalitions</a> with the SPD as well as in state and local-level coalitions with the Alliance '90/The Greens. The CDU rejects coalitions with either <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Far-left" title="Far-left">far-left</a> or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Far-right" title="Far-right">far-right</a> parties.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Free_Democratic_Party_(Germany)" title="Free Democratic Party (Germany)">Free Democratic Party</a> (FDP), a <a href="/wiki/Classical_liberalism" title="Classical liberalism">classical liberal</a> party, is the preferred partner of any CDU government since the CDU and FDP have similar attitudes towards <a href="/wiki/Fiscal_policy" title="Fiscal policy">fiscal policy</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Internal_structure">Internal structure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Christian_Democratic_Union_of_Germany&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Internal structure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Members">Members</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Christian_Democratic_Union_of_Germany&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Members">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In May 2012, the CDU had 484,397 members. The number has dropped by 3.1% in 2011 and 3.0% in 2010. The members' average age was 59 years. 6% of the Christian Democrats were under 30 years old.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-members_May12_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-members_May12-18">[18]</a></sup> A 2007 study by the <a href="/wiki/Konrad_Adenauer_Foundation" title="Konrad Adenauer Foundation">Konrad Adenauer Foundation</a> showed that 25.4% of members were female and 74.6% male. Female participation was higher in the former <a href="/wiki/East_Germany" title="East Germany">East German</a> states with 29.2% compared to 24.8% in the former <a href="/wiki/West_Germany" title="West Germany">West German</a> states.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Die_Mitglieder_der_CDU_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-Die_Mitglieder_der_CDU-19">[19]</a></sup></p>
<p>Before 1966, membership totals in CDU organisation were only estimated. The numbers after 1966 are based on the total from 31 December of the previous year.</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Party_strongholds">Party strongholds</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Christian_Democratic_Union_of_Germany&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Party strongholds">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:CDU_Mitgliederentwicklung.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="630" data-file-width="900" height="210" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/CDU_Mitgliederentwicklung.svg/300px-CDU_Mitgliederentwicklung.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/CDU_Mitgliederentwicklung.svg/450px-CDU_Mitgliederentwicklung.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/CDU_Mitgliederentwicklung.svg/600px-CDU_Mitgliederentwicklung.svg.png 2x" width="300"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:CDU_Mitgliederentwicklung.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Membership development</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The traditional strongholds of the party are concentrated in rural and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Catholic" title="Catholic">Catholic</a> regions such as the <a href="/wiki/Eifel" title="Eifel">Eifel</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/M%C3%BCnsterland" title="Münsterland">Münsterland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sauerland" title="Sauerland">Sauerland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fulda_(district)" title="Fulda (district)">Fulda</a> district, <a href="/wiki/Emsland" title="Emsland">Emsland</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oldenburger_M%C3%BCnsterland" title="Oldenburger Münsterland">Oldenburger Münsterland</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Thuringia" title="Thuringia">Thuringia</a> <a href="/wiki/Eichsfeld" title="Eichsfeld">Eichsfeld</a> as well as areas in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nordfriesland" title="Nordfriesland">Nordfriesland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saxony" title="Saxony">Saxony</a>, <a href="/wiki/Swabia" title="Swabia">Schwaben</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vorpommern" title="Vorpommern">Vorpommern</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saarland" title="Saarland">North Saarland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Taunus" title="Taunus">Taunus</a>, and smaller cities such as <a href="/wiki/Baden-Baden" title="Baden-Baden">Baden-Baden</a>, <a href="/wiki/Konstanz" title="Konstanz">Konstanz</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Pforzheim" title="Pforzheim">Pforzheim</a>. There is less support in <a href="/wiki/Bremen_(state)" title="Bremen (state)">Bremen</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Brandenburg" title="Brandenburg">Brandenburg</a>, and in East <a href="/wiki/Berlin" title="Berlin">Berlin</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Relationship_to_the_CSU">Relationship to the CSU</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Christian_Democratic_Union_of_Germany&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Relationship to the CSU">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation">
<tr>

</td>

<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_B_145_Bild-F074010-0033,_K%C3%B6ln,_Deutschlandtag_Junge_Union.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="532" data-file-width="800" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Bundesarchiv_B_145_Bild-F074010-0033%2C_K%C3%B6ln%2C_Deutschlandtag_Junge_Union.jpg/220px-Bundesarchiv_B_145_Bild-F074010-0033%2C_K%C3%B6ln%2C_Deutschlandtag_Junge_Union.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Bundesarchiv_B_145_Bild-F074010-0033%2C_K%C3%B6ln%2C_Deutschlandtag_Junge_Union.jpg/330px-Bundesarchiv_B_145_Bild-F074010-0033%2C_K%C3%B6ln%2C_Deutschlandtag_Junge_Union.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Bundesarchiv_B_145_Bild-F074010-0033%2C_K%C3%B6ln%2C_Deutschlandtag_Junge_Union.jpg/440px-Bundesarchiv_B_145_Bild-F074010-0033%2C_K%C3%B6ln%2C_Deutschlandtag_Junge_Union.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_B_145_Bild-F074010-0033,_K%C3%B6ln,_Deutschlandtag_Junge_Union.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<i>Germany Day</i> of Junge Union in Cologne, 1986</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Both the CDU and the <a href="/wiki/Christian_Social_Union_in_Bavaria" title="Christian Social Union in Bavaria">Christian Social Union in Bavaria</a> (CSU) originated after World War II, sharing a concern for the Christian worldview. In the Federal Parliament (Bundestag), the CDU is represented in a common faction with the CSU. This faction is called <a href="/wiki/CDU/CSU" title="CDU/CSU">CDU/CSU</a> or, informally, "the Union;" its basis is a binding agreement known as a <i>Fraktionsvertrag</i> between the two parties.</p>
<p>The CDU and CSU share a common youth organisation, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Junge_Union" title="Junge Union">Junge Union</a>.</p>
<p>On issues of federal policies the CDU and CSU do not differ<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>, but they remain legally and organisationally separate parties. The social differences between the CDU and the somewhat more <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Socially_conservative" title="Socially conservative">socially conservative</a> CSU have sometimes been a source of conflict in the past. The most notable and serious such incident was in 1976, when the CSU under <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Franz_Josef_Strau%C3%9F" title="Franz Josef Strauß">Franz Josef Strauß</a> ended the alliance with the CDU at a party conference in Wildbad Kreuth. This decision was reversed shortly thereafter when the CDU threatened to run candidates against the CSU in Bavaria.</p>
<p>The relationship of CDU to the CSU has historic parallels to previous <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Christian_democratic" title="Christian democratic">Christian democratic</a> parties in Germany, with the Catholic <a href="/wiki/Centre_Party_(Germany)" title="Centre Party (Germany)">Centre Party</a> having served as a national Catholic party throughout the <a href="/wiki/German_Empire" title="German Empire">German Empire</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Weimar_Republic" title="Weimar Republic">Weimar Republic</a> with the <a href="/wiki/Bavarian_People%27s_Party" title="Bavarian People's Party">Bavarian People's Party</a> functioning as the Bavarian variant.</p>
<p>Since its formation, the CSU has been more conservative than the CDU. The CSU and the state of Bavaria decided not to sign the <a href="/wiki/Basic_Law_for_the_Federal_Republic_of_Germany" title="Basic Law for the Federal Republic of Germany">Basic Law for the Federal Republic of Germany</a>, as they insisted on more autonomy for the individual <a href="/wiki/States_of_Germany" title="States of Germany">states</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> The CSU and the free state of Bavaria have a separate police and justice system (distinctive and non-federal), and have actively participated in all political affairs of the German Parliament, the German Government, the German Bundesrat, the parliamentary elections of the German President, the European Parliament, and meetings with Gorbachev in Russia.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Konrad_Adenauer_Foundation">Konrad Adenauer Foundation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Christian_Democratic_Union_of_Germany&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Konrad Adenauer Foundation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_B_145_Bild-F053560-0013,_Rh%C3%B6ndorf,_Sitzung_Stiftung_Adenauer-Haus.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="523" data-file-width="800" height="144" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Bundesarchiv_B_145_Bild-F053560-0013%2C_Rh%C3%B6ndorf%2C_Sitzung_Stiftung_Adenauer-Haus.jpg/220px-Bundesarchiv_B_145_Bild-F053560-0013%2C_Rh%C3%B6ndorf%2C_Sitzung_Stiftung_Adenauer-Haus.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Bundesarchiv_B_145_Bild-F053560-0013%2C_Rh%C3%B6ndorf%2C_Sitzung_Stiftung_Adenauer-Haus.jpg/330px-Bundesarchiv_B_145_Bild-F053560-0013%2C_Rh%C3%B6ndorf%2C_Sitzung_Stiftung_Adenauer-Haus.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Bundesarchiv_B_145_Bild-F053560-0013%2C_Rh%C3%B6ndorf%2C_Sitzung_Stiftung_Adenauer-Haus.jpg/440px-Bundesarchiv_B_145_Bild-F053560-0013%2C_Rh%C3%B6ndorf%2C_Sitzung_Stiftung_Adenauer-Haus.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_B_145_Bild-F053560-0013,_Rh%C3%B6ndorf,_Sitzung_Stiftung_Adenauer-Haus.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Conference in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rh%C3%B6ndorf" title="Rhöndorf">Rhöndorf</a>, with eminent historian <a href="/wiki/Golo_Mann" title="Golo Mann">Golo Mann</a> (center), 1978</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Konrad_Adenauer_Foundation" title="Konrad Adenauer Foundation">Konrad Adenauer Foundation</a> is the think-tank of the CDU. It is named after the first Chancellor of the Federal Republic of Germany and first president of the CDU. The foundation offers political education, conducts scientific fact-finding research for political projects, grants scholarships to gifted individuals, researches the history of <a href="/wiki/Christian_democracy" title="Christian democracy">Christian democracy</a>, and supports and encourages <a href="/wiki/European_integration" title="European integration">European unification</a>, international understanding, and development-policy cooperation. Its annual budget amounts to around 120 million Euro.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Special_organizations">Special organizations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Christian_Democratic_Union_of_Germany&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Special organizations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Notable suborganisations of the CDU are:</p>
<ul>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Junge_Union" title="Junge Union">Junge Union</a> (JU), the common youth organisation of the CDU and the CSU;</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Christian_Democratic_Employees%27_Association" title="Christian Democratic Employees' Association">Christian Democratic Employees' Association</a> (CDA), a traditionally leftist association representing Christian Democratic wage-earners;</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Evangelical_Working_Group_of_the_CDU/CSU" title="Evangelical Working Group of the CDU/CSU">Evangelical Working Group of the CDU/CSU</a> (EAK, together with the CSU), representing the Protestant minority in the party;</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Association_of_Christian_Democratic_Students" title="Association of Christian Democratic Students">Association of Christian Democratic Students</a> (RCDS), the student organisation of the party.</li>
</ul>
